212. Re: FMC rules
From: "Gilles Roux" <grrroux@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 02 Jun 2006 15:53:31 -0000

A limited time as the WCA format would be a good thing. 1 hour is long enough to try a few solutions with a good start. Spending more time makes you find better solutions - because you can explore more and find lucky tricks, - and because you can think more and use your science of cubing. But my opinion is that a high level in cube science should make you find any useful information in less then 1 hour. Exceeding this time means you're relying on luck to heavily. Cheating by luck. Gilles. --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...> wrote: > > Hi :-) > > If i spend 100 hrs on a fmc challenge it's not cheating! Stupidity > yes :-P Looking up some alg that i don't know is cheating (unless i > can construct it from basic principles). Just read Dan's fmc > regulations :-) > > Cheers! > > > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Gilles Roux" > <grrroux@> wrote: > > > > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Daniel Harris" > > <dan_j_harris@> wrote: > > > > > > > If you can, imagine that you are in a real WCA > > > competition scenario. > > > > A real WCA competition is very different. You have LIMITED TIME! > > > > Who's the worst cheater, a cuber who has a few tables or a cuber > who > > can spend 30 hours finding a lucky solution? > > > > Gilles. > > >

217. Insertions
From: "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 03 Jun 2006 08:06:37 -0000

Insertion is a very simple idea to understand, not quite as simple to put into practice, but if you work at it it will suddenly click :) I will give an example of the simplest possible insertion, probably stolen from one of Per's solutions... ( I haven't searched yet ;) ) The scramble: U' D (L B2 D' L2 F)*4 B' U' R2 B F' (R' U B2 U2 L)*4 B R After searching, Per somehow magically came up with the very short base solution L F' D L2 U' F D' B' R2 B2 U.F2 U' L' The above sequence solves everything but for 3 corners. You could of course then use a commutator at the end of the move sequence to solve those 3 corners, but it is usually more beneficial to backtrack through the solution, while following those 3 corners. The reason for doing this, is that at any point during the solve where you could solve the corner 3-cycle using a commutator, there is a possibility that moves in your "insertion" would cancel out with moves in your original solve, thus being more efficient. The idea is simple, but I found it very hard to put into practice, so maybe more specialist people could also give their input :) Per inserted U' B D2 B' U B D2 B' at the dot, so you can see that U U' cancelled, and then B2 B combined into B', to cancel 3 moves, giving a 19 move solution. (14 move start + 8 move commutator - 3 cancelled moves) Using insertions is a clever way of reducing the number of moves you need to solve a 3-cycle of corners. I believe it can be used for edge cycles too, but I have never used it. I think that to master it requires a lot of experience, so don't be frustrated if you can't see it right away! Dan :) --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "fonnny" <dan@...> wrote: > > Thanks Cyril. I had actually just read that the other night. I'm not > sure if I'm just slow :-) or if I'm missing some of the building > blocks to even be able to fully understand what that post means! > > Does anybody have a pointer or some examples of what an "insertion" is? > > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Cyril Castella" > <cyrilca@> wrote: > > > > Hi ! > > Two things before I go to bed ... > > > > > Is there a tutorial or starters guide for some of these "tricks of > > the trade"? > > > > ---> Then you may be interested in this message : > > http://games.groups.yahoo.com/group/fewestmoveschallenge/message/853 > > (Richard's and my propositions concerning this question) > > > > The other thing I wanted to say is ... congratulations to Tim for your > > insertion in the same basic solution as me, you proved you are smarter > > than me with your STM move gain ;-) Too bad I did not see it, we could > > have submitted exactly the same solutions (I remember this has been > > discussed once here do anyone remember if it has ever happened in FMC > > history ?) > > > > Good luck with #108, I'm too stressed to give it a go, see you for the > > next challenges ! > > > > cyril > > >

219. Re: Insertions
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 03 Jun 2006 15:35:26 -0000

Hi :-) I would say that inserting ONE corner 3-cycle into a skeleton solution is quite straight forward. Once the concept of ceorrectly labelling the 3 required corners correctly with sticker (such that cycling them according to the stickers will rotate them correctly as well). Quite another matter is to insert say a corner 5-cycle. First of all more stickers are required. There is more possible cycles to look out for. And inserting the "best first" 3-cycle is not guarantee for overall best insertion. The 5-cycle is broken down into 2 3-cycles that are inserted individually :-) As for inserting edge-cycle it's not any harder in principle, but the abundance of edge 3-cycle algs is quite overwhelming. It's easier to keep track of corner 3-cycle algs. And besides, i find it generally easier to solve edges first and then corners later. Rather than the opposite approach. That said i have indeed had solutions that end with edge-insertions :-) Cheers! -Per PS! Don't be put off by 14 moves with 3 corners left. That was a really rare case, where i got 2 solved corners for free while arranging the edges :-) > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...> wrote: > > Insertion is a very simple idea to understand, not quite as simple to > put into practice, but if you work at it it will suddenly click :) > > I will give an example of the simplest possible insertion, probably > stolen from one of Per's solutions... 223. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: FMC rules
From: Ryan Heise <ryan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 4 Jun 2006 11:49:41 +1000

On Fri, Jun 02, 2006 at 03:53:31PM -0000, Gilles Roux wrote: > > A limited time as the WCA format would be a good thing. 1 hour is long > enough to try a few solutions with a good start. > > Spending more time makes you find better solutions > - because you can explore more and find lucky tricks, > - and because you can think more and use your science of cubing. But > my opinion is that a high level in cube science should make you find > any useful information in less then 1 hour. Exceeding this time means > you're relying on luck to heavily. Cheating by luck. Having second attempts is also cheating by luck ;-) If "luck" means receiving good fortune by chance, then one way to reduce luck is to reduce the number of chances down to just 1. It is still possible to be lucky, given just one chance, so the next step is to take an average over a series of separate challenges. I have an idea for another format which can be run in parallel to the FMC, if there is any interest: - 5 scrambles, 5 minutes per scramble, 1 attempt per scramble. - Average the 5 solution lengths (or the best 3 out of 5?) As for FMC, yes I think a 1 hour limit is better than a 168 hour limit, but there is no reason why both formats could not run in parallel on the same scramble. -- Ryan Heise http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/

231. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: FMC rules
From: Ryan Heise <ryan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 5 Jun 2006 11:21:34 +1000

On Sun, Jun 04, 2006 at 02:11:32PM -0000, Per Kristen Fredlund wrote: > > As for FMC, yes I think a 1 hour limit is better than a 168 hour > > limit, but there is no reason why both formats could not run in > > parallel on the same scramble. > > How would that be possible? Then i just wait participating in the 1 hr > version until i have something really good. - Spend the first hour searching for a solution. - After 1 hour submit your best solution. - Then, continue searching for an even better solution. - After 1 week submit your even better solution as well. i.e. two submissions for the same scramble. > And one more idea. For a 1 hr time-limited challenge u can with ur > system log what time a participant is opening the challenge. Then use > that info to actually limit when he/she can submit also. So that it's > impossible to spend excessive time on it. I like that idea! Sounds > feasible to me :-) To prevent cheating, every person would have to start the challenge at the same time, otherwise two people (or possibly one person with two email addresses) could collude by one person letting the other one know what the scramble is before they open the challenge. Another way to prevent this could be to provide each person a different scramble, but I don't think this is fair for FMC, since some scrambles seem easier than others. On the other hand, that problem can be solved by taking averages.. -- Ryan Heise http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/
232. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] 60min fmc

Thanks to everyone who has been kind enough to comment on the new system, thus far I haven't had too many problems to deal with. However, has anyone using a Mac had trouble with the FMC pages? Oh well :) It looks like there are few 14 move solutions to that in Helmstetter (1017 is the inverse, I think), which would probably put the total at 28. Not that I intend to memorize all that. Final layer positions like that are pretty thankless with all 8 pieces "on the loose". You have to find some way to fix the edges AND one corner somewhere to get down to a 3 corner commutator. There isn't much "wiggle room" in this start either. Normally, you can insert a few random moves here and there that doesn't affect the block you're building, but here a lot of the moves are forced. > and a pseudo F2L in 14 moves > R' B F2 L B' D' R B L B' U' B' R [U], where the move in the bracket > can be prepended to the scrambling moves. 243. Re: FMC #113 (Post-modification)
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 09 Jul 2006 16:22:36 -0000

Hi Charles ! (and all) I had overlooked Charles' easy start. Studying his start i came up with the following: F R2 D' R' B D2 B for a pseudoblock > add D2 premove to scramble. Now continue F R F' F2 > add another premove R' to scramble. Now finish edges with F' D' F D, leaving 5 corners. Now D' L D R' D' L' D R solves 3 corners and cancels 2 moves. Adjust for the premoves by adding R' D2 and 3 more moves cancel nicely! Then we have : F R2 D' R' B D2 B F R F' R2 F' D'.F L D R' D' L' D' with 3 corners to go. Now either add (D2 L' U2 L)*2 at the end to cancel 1 move for a direct 27-move solution. Or, insert D L' U L D' L' U' L at the dot for a 26-move solution. The latter also gives excellent sub-30 qtm. The good start did it all :-) Cheers! -Per

It is D2 L' U F R' F2 D B' L B U L R' U . Does any of you have a table showing how many different positions can be reached in 14 or less moves? What is the probability that a random scrambled position can be solved in less than 15 moves? It must be very low. Mirek
251. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] FMC 116 in 14 moves
From: Lars Petrus <lars@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 2 Aug 2006 22:58:31 -0700

I don't have a table, but if you assume that 18 is the norm, and there are 15 moves in each position, and negligible duplication, you'd end up with one chance in 15^4 = 50625 to get a 14 mover. Pretty shaky assumptions, I know. If anyone has any better, do let us know. In 116 competitions, that would mean we'd have about 0.2% for this to occur randomly. /Lars On Aug 2, 2006, at 19:17, mirek_goljan wrote: > Hi, everybody, > did you notice that the cube scramble was unusually of "low > complexity"? 255. #119 FMC : my partial solution
From: "Cyril Castella" <cyrilca@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 21 Aug 2006 07:19:30 -0000

Hi, I did not have enough time to participate, but I found an interesting start for #119 FMC and thought that I could share it with you here. Suggestions are welcome, especially for smarter "R move" insertion and/or corners cycle :-) Have fun, Cyril Scramble : (F B' R2 D)*3 L2 U D' B2 (F' R U2)*4 L D' U B (U2 L F' R2)*3 Solution (2 flipped edges, 26 HTM-24 STM) : U B2 D {L' R} {F B'} R' B2 L2 U' F' U2 B' F' R F' U B2 U' F U B2 U' F R2 Quote : Partial solution only. Had not much time but I found this very interesting start for F2L minus one pair in 13 HTM: UB2DL'.F. B'R'B2L2U'F'U2B' The miracle is that it is possible to insert any R- slice move at the first OR the second dot. R at the first dot does it, since F2L are solved with an additional F'R|F. Insert (F'UB2U'FUB2U') at the colon for the corners (I was lazy) and you get UB2DL'(R) FB'R'B2L2U'F'U2B'F'R (F'UB2U'FUB2U') FR2: 26 HTM ... but 2 flipped edges. My solution would be too long if flip them, so I leave it as a partial solution :)
256. Scrambles and competitions
From: "Gilles Roux" <grrroux@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 24 Aug 2006 22:06:24 -0000

In WCA competition regulations (http://www.speedcubing.com/events/regulations.html) Article E, nothing special is said about scrambling for a fewest-moves events. Normal scrambles of Article E apply. 3x3x3 -> 25-move scrambling sequence. In Dan's FMC tradition, sequences are made of about 50 moves, based on the repetition of macros. In the past, I wondered why, because: - I *think* 25 moves are enough to generate a perfectly randomized cube state, many more random than with curiously generated macros. Or else, it must be changed for speedcubing rules too. - Applying a "difficult to remember and execute" 25-move sequence is in my opinion faster than 50-move one with not-so-easy macros separated by alien moves. - I was thinking before that, maybe, with only 25 moves, people could find a good solution inspired by the scramble. I changed my mind, because it's not that easy after all. Of course, "(scramble)'U'U" is easy to find, that's why something's said about being able to explain the solution. What are your ideas about what the official FMC scrambling technique should be: - Standard random 25-moves. - Generated by a different technique. - Random X-moves. - I don't care! After all, any technique can produce easy cubes, absolute FMC records do not matter, only event winning people! Gilles. P.S.: I often considered the word "algorithm" was inadequately used by cubers. For me, an algorithm is a step-by-step understandable problem-solving procedure. You can guess the expression "scrambling algorithm" makes my blood boil, because if an algorithm is needed, it's only for having a method that generates random numbers, deep inside function random().

I think 25 moves is good. Don't understand why those looooooooooooooooong algs on fewest moves...just makes things harder (to scramble, of course) : ) Pedro Gilles Roux <grrroux@...> escreveu: In WCA competition regulations (http://www.speedcubing.com/events/regulations.html) Article E, nothing special is said about scrambling for a fewest-moves events. Normal scrambles of Article E apply. 3x3x3 -> 25-move scrambling sequence. In Dan's FMC tradition, sequences are made of about 50 moves, based on the repetition of macros. In the past, I wondered why, because: - I *think* 25 moves are enough to generate a perfectly randomized cube state, many more random than with curiously generated macros. Or else, it must be changed for speedcubing rules too. - Applying a "difficult to remember and execute" 25-move sequence is in my opinion faster than 50-move one with not-so-easy macros separated by alien moves. - I was thinking before that, maybe, with only 25 moves, people could find a good solution inspired by the scramble. I changed my mind, because it's not that easy after all. Of course, "(scramble)'U'U" is easy to find, that's why something's said about being able to explain the solution. What are your ideas about what the official FMC scrambling technique should be: - Standard random 25-moves. - Generated by a different technique. - Random X-moves. - I don't care! After all, any technique can produce easy cubes, absolute FMC records do not matter, only event winning people! Gilles. P.S.: I often considered the word "algorithm" was inadequately used by cubers. For me, an algorithm is a step-by-step understandable problem-solving procedure. You can guess the expression "scrambling algorithm" makes my blood boil, because if an algorithm is needed, it's only for having a method that generates random numbers, deep inside function random(). --------------------------------- VocÂ¤ quer respostas para suas perguntas? Ou vocÂ¤ sabe muito e quer compartilhar seu conhecimento? Experimente o Yahoo! Respostas!

Hi Dan, I like your start for FMC #120. To remind you the scramble, it was U' B2 L B' R2 U2 B' D' U2 F L' R D2 F U B2 L F2 R2 B F U' D F L You did 2x2x3 block as D' F D2 R' U R2 B' L2 B2. I spent about 15 minutes to find the following. Begin with your 6 moves D' F D2 R' U R2, here I opt for making another corner-edge pair as F L' F'. Then finish 2x2x3 B' L2 B2, fix another pair L' D2 L and now a little trick F' B' D F D' B D and only 3 corners left after 22 moves (HTM). Unfortunately, I don't see an insertion of a corner 3 cycle better than D2 L' U' L D2 L' U L after the L2 move. Alltogether, it's D' F D2 R' U R2 F L' F' B' L2 (D2 L' U' L D2 L' U L) B2 L' D2 L F' B' D F D' B D. (29 HTM) Happy cubing! Mirek

269. Re: Looking for more information for FMC?
From: "Cyril Castella" <cyrilca@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 18 Sep 2006 12:46:02 -0000

Hi James, There are not many websites about GMC techniques, some posts here may give you a good basis : http://games.groups.yahoo.com/group/fewestmoveschallenge/message/852 http://games.groups.yahoo.com/group/fewestmoveschallenge/message/854 and so on ... The idea with insertions is that is it often shorter to solve "nearly" every cubie than the whole cube. Then you insert a corner or an edge cycle in the "near-solution" to fix the remaining pieces. The good thing with insertions is that you can usually cancel some moves if you find a good place. You can use PLL's for cycling edges or corners, but there are some algs (commutators) that are usually shorter and that are often easier to insert. The stickers are useful to follow the pieces that you want to cycle throughout your "near- solution", and see when they have the right configuration. It takes time, but it is really cool when you can for example replace a 20+ moves OLL + PLL by 1 corner cycle and 1 edges cycle, saving some moves, and ending with a 10-12 moves LL :) Last thing ... none of us uses Acube or algs table ;-) Just take some time to read the posts I mentioned above, google commutators+rubik and be prepared to spend some hours on the scrambles ! Good luck, Cyril --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "James Straughan" <athefre@...> wrote: > > Last week's FMC (123) was my first try but I didn't feel like I knew > what I was doing. I don't see any information on Dan's site. I read > some of the comments for past FMCs and they were talking about some > things I don't know about. 273. Re: Looking for more information for FMC?
From: "Cyril Castella" <cyrilca@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 20 Sep 2006 11:10:36 -0000

Hi James, Just some more comments on your questions. Lars gave really helpful answers ... > 1. What's a premove? I've read stuff about doing moves to the cube > before you scramble, that seems like cheating. > 2. Setup moves? Actually it's the same thing. Suppose you have a block approach like Petrus', you find a lovely 2x2x2 block but no good possibility to extend it to a 2x2x3. Instead, you may find easier to finish a 2x2x1 block that does NOT belong to the 2x2x3, and place it next to your 2x2x2. You now have a pseudo-block (pseudo 2x2x3 in this case). There are now two possibities: A) You are really smart and you are not disturbed by the fact the color do not match and you continue to solve the cube B) You are like us and you prefer when colors match. So you simply add the move that would place the non-matching pieces of your pseudo block BEFORE scrambling, and the miracle will happen: the colors will now match. In your final submission, you will however still have to add the inverse of the setup move (= premove) after your solution in order to solve the real scramble. For example, see Dan's #120 solution : D' F D2 R' U R2 B' L2 B2 D' F D2 R' U R2 solve pseudo-F2L, but if you add D2 before scrambling you'll see "true F2L", which is much easier for figuring out the LL :) Actually it is NOT cheating, since you still end up with a moves sequence that solves the given scamble ! Hope this helps ... > 6. Last thing, can I have an explanation of the reason for > putting "." or ":" in your comments for FMC and saying you inserted > something there? I need a better explanation of this and insertions. Well, it's just a simple way to indicate where you inserted the cycle. Actually easier than saying "I inserted the corner cycle after the 4th D2" or "... after the 23rd move" ;) > Sorry, I just want to know all of these terms so I can do better and > so I don't sound stupid when explaining things. I don't know how > everyone else knows this. I did search the forums but since I don't > know much I can't find the right posts. You're not stupid at all, or I am too ! I had the same questions when I started doing FMC. I thought that the others were adding random premoves to make the scramble easier ! Good luck ;) cyril
274. Re: Looking for more information for FMC?
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 20 Sep 2006 14:18:02 -0000

Hi :-) Finally an interesting thread on this forum. One about ... umm ... fewest moves ... lol ;-) Premoves are related to pseudoblocks. Let me explain what it's all about. Take a solved cube and do R then (DB) couple of times to mess up the cube a bit. U know have a pseudoblock (2x2x3) at the UF position. Say u had arrived at that configuration after n moves in ur solution. And now u wish that the 2x2x3 block was PURE (so that u can see more clearly what to do with the rest of the cubies). In this case write down ur n moves (or use the Fewest Move Companion). Now set up the scramble again but do an additional R' at the start first. Now ur n turns will set up a PURE 2x2x3 block. It's not too hard to understand how this works when thinking about it :-) Now this example only used ONE premove. I have seen 2 premoves used in solutions, but only 1 is usually sufficient. Or possibly u arrive at a situation where u want to do 1 premove and then a bit later again u add one more. It all depends. Just remember that the solution u end with is solution to an incorrect scramble (it has premoves). So adjust for this by adding some turns in the end. U easily see what those additional moves are anyway ;-) I am not sure if this has been mentioned already. But one extra trick of the trade (that i have never used successfully) is to instead do the reverse of the scramble and solve that configuration (with all normal tricks used). Then when u have ur solution just reverse it. This reversed solution is the solution to the ORIGINAL scramble. Also quite easy to understand why it must be so ;-) Finally about cycles there is more to it than just tracking positions. A 3-cycle can be PURE or twisted. Ok, let me explain this. Do following 3-cycle on a solved cube : R' D' R U' R' D R U. This is a PURE 3-cycle. The 3 corners can be correctly solved by a corner 3-cycle. In this case that cycle is just the reverse of the given moves. Now say u did some alg that flipped 2 corners. One of them being a corner involved in the cycle and one which is NOT. Now there is NO WAY to correctly solve those 3 corners with just a 3- cycle. No matter what u do 1 or more of them will be incorrectly oriented!! U might wonder if doing a corner 2-twist then a 3-cycle is the best way to solve this? I would generally say NO! There is a better way. Can u see how? The generally best way is to correctly solve 1 of those 3 corners that u cycled first. Do this by a 3-cycle (yes!!) but one that involves just 2 of the corners u cycled first but also involved the lonely twisted corner :D If done correctly u now have one more PURE corner 3-cycle to do. This should i guess always be the best approach. As a note i can mention that u could also do a corner 2-twist as 2 3-cycles. I leave it up to u to see how ;-) The point about insertion and stickers is that it's quite easy to "track" ur 3 corner a few moves backwards from the end of ur "skeleton" solution. But it's damn hard to track them many moves back. And even if u track positions correctly, tracking orientations is much harder. That's why it's good to put stickers on the cubies of interest, the cubies u are gonna find insertion alg for. Now insertion would NOT be of much use if one didn't try to insert at a point where u will get move cancellations. A corner 3-cycle done at the end would maybe take 8 turns, or possibly more ... Unless rare case an inserted corner 3-cycle takes 7 additional moves or less. I have managed once to insert corner 5-cycle in only 7 additional moves. A rare case yes, but worth looking for, with stickers!! Best of luck, -Per (PS! The more options u are exploring the better the chance for finding something GOOD :D The luck-factor;-) ) > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, Lars Petrus <lars@...> wrote: > > On Sep 19, 2006, at 22:13, James Straughan wrote: > > > I read through all of the posts that were part of the ones you gave. > > I also went to Ryan Heise's site and read his commutators section. I > > could solve them on my own except for the last one, it's a little > > different from the others he described. > > > > 1. What's a premove? I've read stuff about doing moves to the cube > > before you scramble, that seems like cheating. > FMC is all about cheating, in that you get to redo and redo the same > solution as many times as you can. > > 2. Setup moves? > Setup moves? > > 3. I still don't understand the point of stickers, do people really > > have a hard time remembering what they are doing? > Yes they do. But that's not what the stickers are for. > > The stickers are for insertions. When you understand insertions, you > will understand the need for stickers. Before you understand > insertions, don't worry about the stickers. > > 4. 5-cycles? 3-cycles? > N-cycle: Algorithm that moves only n pieces. > > 5. I did some google searches but every site I saw (except Ryan's > > page) described stuff very mathematically. > > 6. Last thing, can I have an explanation of the reason for > > putting "." or ":" in your comments for FMC and saying you inserted > > something there? I'm not sure how > to explain it better to you than your own words do. If you use premoves, you can make it look like a real 2x2x3. Try (DB)*10 without the R before those moves, now it's a real 2x2x3. This is the difference between pseudoblocks and real blocks. > >Finally about cycles... > > >One of > >them being a corner involved in the cycle and one which is NOT. Involved in what cycle? Does "3- > cycle" mean "cycle 3 corners"? So is there a "2-cycle" for 2 corners? Yes, 3-cycle means cycle 3 corners. In Per's example, there was one 3-cycle and one corner in its right place, but twisted. The best way is to first do one 3-cycle that solves one corner and leaves 3 other corners to cycle. I'm not an expert, but I hope this makes sense... > >Now say u did some alg that flipped 2 corners. > > Are you saying flip 2 corners AFTER I've done R' D' R U' R' D R U? > Or was that something not related to the moving 3 corners alg above. > Does that make sense? Exactly, first you would solve UFL, UFR or DFR with a 3-cycle that also involves the UBL-corner. RB'R'F'RBR'F, for example. Now you are left with one more 3-cycle. > >U might wonder if doing a corner 2-twist then a 3-cycle is the best > >way to solve this? I would generally say NO! There is a better way. > >Can u see how? That was a little hard... > > So if I AM left with 4 corners in you are talking about, is the best > way to solve 2 corners at a time (2-cycle?, 2-twist?) (like in the > above solution)? I think the best way is to solve *one* corner, so that you are left with a 3-cycle. > > >The point about insertion and stickers is that it's quite easy > >to "track" ur 3 corner a few moves backwards from the end of > >ur "skeleton" solution. Why? No. First, you create the skeleton solution that leaves 3 corners to solve, for example. Then you mark those corners with stickers. 277. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: Looking for more information for FMC?
From: Ryan Heise <ryan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 21 Sep 2006 23:37:33 +1000

Cyril Castella wrote: > You now have a pseudo-block (pseudo 2x2x3 in this case). There > are now two possibities: > A) You are really smart and you are not disturbed by the fact the > color do not match and you continue to solve the cube > B) You are like us and you prefer when colors match. This depends on whether the misalignment is off by 90 degrees or 180 degrees. It also depends on the underlying method being used. - A misalignment of 90 degrees makes orientation cases difficult to recognise in most methods, while a misalignment of 180 degrees is fairly easy to get used to. - However, a method designed to take advantage of non-matching blocks might not have the same problems. e.g.: http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/method/stage1.html I use this approach in speedcubing, so it certainly isn't so difficult that you would need to be "really smart" to do it. This approach was designed for "normal" solving (i.e. solving from beginning to end, and not beginning -> end -> middle, or end -> middle -> beginning, as many FMC people like to do - I don't), so it can be done without "premoves". Examples of this solving approach can be found here: http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/method/ http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/speed.html (in my average record) -- Ryan Heise http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/

281. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] 3 corner, orient only
From: Ryan Heise <ryan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 11:20:45 +1000

jjallan303 wrote: > Does anyone do anything smart when they end up with 3 corners in the > correct location, yet in the incorrect orientation - I guess one could > conjugate and do LL for this case, but I think that would be pretty > long. There are only 3 cases. Dare I say it, you could memorise some optimal solutions instead of solving it yourself. What I do is combine two commutators. This is usually about 15 moves, which is "almost" optimal. > Does anyone else ignore this solution, put it down to bad luck, and > get on with their next iteration of their search? In FMC, or real life? - In real life, when people want to see how many moves I take, they say I'm a cheat if I begin un-doing moves and trying alternatives, as if there were some obvious rules. - In FMC, I'm sure lots of people do this, because the rules allow it. Under these rules, the cube is not viewed as a game that you play move by move, but is instead viewed as a "graph", and the goal being to use a search algorithm to find the shortest path within that graph between one node and another. In context, these rules make no sense to me. The 3 twisted corners case is certainly a bad case, but is only bad luck if you were not trying to avoid it. -- Ryan Heise http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/

Two corner 3-cycles should generally be the best way, but is harder than twisting 2 corners only w 2 3-cycles :-) Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "jjallan303" <jjallan@...> wrote: > > > jjallan303 wrote: > > > > > Does anyone do anything smart when they end up with 3 corners in the > > > correct location, yet in the incorrect orientation - I guess one could > > > conjugate and do LL for this case, but I think that would be pretty > > > long. > > > > There are only 3 cases. Dare I say it, you could memorise some optimal > > solutions instead of solving it yourself. > > Yes I guess... > Acording to good ol' Cube Explorer, the 3, ignoring symmetries, in > generator form, are: > 1) D F' U' B U' B U' F U2 B2 D' R2 U (13f) > 2) F' U2 B2 D B' U B' U B' D' B F R2 (13f) > 3) U' B U' F U' F U' B' D U R2 D' F2 U' (14f) > > > > > What I do is combine two commutators. This is usually about 15 moves, > > which is "almost" optimal. > > This sounds good, less memory, and if one finds two good insertion > points then it may be better than the above! > > > > > > Does anyone else ignore this solution, put it down to bad luck, and > > > get on with their next iteration of their search? > > > > In FMC, or real life? > > FMC - now I know this can be solved in 13 moves P=2/3 or 14 P=1/3, I > guess most of the time I find it I would plain ignore it - as ct > commented if the path there was short (I'd say <19) it may be worth > finding a useful insertion point. > > > > - In real life, when people want to see how many moves I take, they say > > I'm a cheat if I begin un-doing moves and trying alternatives, as if > > there were some obvious rules. > > - In FMC, I'm sure lots of people do this, because the rules allow it. > > Under these rules, the cube is not viewed as a game that you play move > > by move, but is instead viewed as a "graph", and the goal being to use > > a search algorithm to find the shortest path within that graph between > > one node and another. In context, these rules make no sense to me. > > > > I agree with your point - remember most people who can do the cube, > given the challenge to do it in FMC rules, would not shave much off > their average. So just give them two averages (say, 61 moves for WCA > standard solving, but 34 under WCA FMC rules). > > > > The 3 twisted corners case is certainly a bad case, but is only bad luck > > if you were not trying to avoid it. > > > > -- > > Ryan Heise > > http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/ > > >

286. My EC2006 FMC
From: "Gilles Roux" <grrroux@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 25 Sep 2006 11:40:49 -0000

Yesterday, 7 competitors found a 1-hour solution in 36 moves or less. I suppose the scramble was not difficult. You may want to have a look at it: RD'B'L2R2B2L'R'DL2B2D'LB'F2LUFD'L'R'D2B'F'D I found my winning 31-move solution in about 20 minutes: S'zDL2D' (left block) F'RL2B'LRU' (right block) x'L2URU'LU (corners - B5 case) rR2 (last 6 edges orientation) U'MU2M' (insert UL+UR) U'MU2R2 (M-permutation) Overall, I got about 10 sub-40 solutions: 31, 32, 34, 36 and worse. Congratulations to those who achieved good results, with maybe less luck than I had, especially those who managed to insert 3-cycles (waiting for Dan's comment). Gilles.

288. Dan's EC2006 FMC
From: "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 26 Sep 2006 09:39:22 -0000

Gilles said: > Yesterday, 7 competitors found a 1-hour solution in 36 moves or less. > I suppose the scramble was not difficult. > > You may want to have a look at it: > RD'B'L2R2B2L'R'DL2B2D'LB'F2LUFD'L'R'D2B'F'D So, here is my solution, as transcribed from my awful scrawly notes ;) There were two nice looking blocks at the start, one on F, and one on U. It took me a minute to notice that you could form a 2x2x3 with these. I tried something like L U2 F' L' U' F' L U F' U B' D B U' before settling on: L U2 F' L' U' L U L' F2 U B2 U' forms a 2x2x3, not pseudo. Now I try to solve all edges, and hope that something good happens to the corners. F L2 F' takes care of the remaining edge on the U face. I then solve the remaining edges two generator style - D' B D2 B' D2. I found this fairly quickly, but then tried to look for other solutions solving more corners, perhaps wasting 15 minutes finding nothing. so we have L U2 F' L' U' L U L' F2 U B2 U' F L2 F' D' B D2 B' D2 leaving two pure corner 3-cycles, which can be solved with two insertions. Right at the end I solved one corner cycle with D' B' U B D B' U' B cancelling 1 move now we have L U2 F' L' U' L U L' F2 U B2 U' F L2 F' D' B D2 B' D B' U B D B' . U' B and inserting F' U' B2 U F U' B2 U at the dot cancels another 3 moves leaving the final 32 move solution L U2 F' L' U' L U L' F2 U B2 U' F L2 F' D' B D2 B' D B' U B D B' F' U' B2 U F U' B' - 32 HTM Dan :)

297. Improving last layer :-)
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 01 Oct 2006 17:18:04 -0000

Hi Eric :-) I read ur comment to last weeks fewest moves challenge. Ur start is actually very good :-) After 12 turns u have solved first 2 layers minus one corner. Apart from this ur best help is maybe actually to break away from thinking u have to do f2l then last layer for fewest moves. What u are doing is to solve 20 cubies, no more and no less. There is many many ways to do this. And i dare say that thinking f2l>solved is in general not very productive for fewest moves. Especially if ur knowledge about last layer does not stretch far beyond OLL/PLL. Now back to ur solution, first 12 turns : B' U D L' D' L2 B R' B' F' D F. If u know do D2 u have an easy 6-move alg that solves the edges for u : F L D L' D' F'. This algorithm is always very handy. Forward or backwards or mirrored ... Interestingly in this case we can do much better by helping with a simple setup move : R. So now instead of simply F L D L' D' F' we do R F L D L' D' F' R'. And magically we have solved 2 more corners. So my point is, learn not only how the edges move for F L D L' D' F'-like algs, but also how corners move. And use this knowledge together with setup-moves for sometimes very good results. Note that in addition to setup moves before F L D L' D' F' one can also insert a move of U layer after the first turn for other effects on the corners .. and so on ... So ur solution is now : B' U D L' D' L2 B R' B' F' D F D2 R F L D L' D' F' R'. 21 turns and only a corner 3-cycle left. This should be dealt with by insertion. Read earlier posts about this or contact me :-) Cheers! -Per

And mine first 9 moves are not that good per :) ~AO --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...> wrote: > > Hi Eric :-) > > I read ur comment to last weeks fewest moves challenge. > > Ur start is actually very good :-) After 12 turns u have solved > first 2 layers minus one corner. Apart from this ur best help is > maybe actually to break away from thinking u have to do f2l then > last layer for fewest moves. What u are doing is to solve 20 cubies, > no more and no less. There is many many ways to do this. And i dare > say that thinking f2l>solved is in general not very productive for > fewest moves. Especially if ur knowledge about last layer does not > stretch far beyond OLL/PLL. > > Now back to ur solution, first 12 turns : B' U D L' D' L2 B R' B' F' > D F. If u know do D2 u have an easy 6-move alg that solves the edges > for u : F L D L' D' F'. This algorithm is always very handy. Forward > or backwards or mirrored ... Interestingly in this case we can do > much better by helping with a simple setup move : R. So now instead > of simply F L D L' D' F' we do R F L D L' D' F' R'. And magically we > have solved 2 more corners. So my point is, learn not only how the > edges move for F L D L' D' F'-like algs, but also how corners move. > And use this knowledge together with setup-moves for sometimes very > good results. Note that in addition to setup moves before F L D L' > D' F' one can also insert a move of U layer after the first turn for > other effects on the corners .. and so on ... > > So ur solution is now : B' U D L' D' L2 B R' B' F' D F > D2 R F L D L' D' F' R'. 21 turns and only a corner 3-cycle left. > This should be dealt with by insertion. Read earlier posts about > this or contact me :-) > > Cheers! > > -Per >

311. Re: Provisional?
From: "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 30 Oct 2006 08:29:31 -0000

Hi Eric, The "numbers" are a rating calculated from your previous 6 performances. Those 6 performances can be seen underneath your solution, and the current week is highlighted in bold. If you haven't solved 6 cubes yet, then your rating would be provisional. There are no strict boundaries, but I would suggest that 800+ is grandmaster, 700+ expert, 500+ advanced, 400+ intermediate, and <400 beginner. Dan :) --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...> wrote: > > what do the numbers mean? 315. Re: A note to Per's FMC #131
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 23 Nov 2006 17:32:41 -0000

Hey! I finally took some time to look at it again. I gain a slice turn whichever way actually ... 1) L' R' B' R U L U F' D' F2 D' B U' D2 [F2 U U' F'>]F D F U [F' D' F + F' D F] D' R D F' D' F R'>>...{UD'}... 2) L' R' B' R U L U F' D' F2 D' B U' D2 [F2 U U' F'>]F D F U F' [D' F+ F' D] B D' F D B' D'>> ...{F'B}... So they are equal in every metric actually, but option 1 comes from a better cancellation, so i think it's cooler anyway :D -Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...> wrote: > > Per, > you mastered edges+at_least_2corners approach. 316. Edges First....
From: "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 26 Nov 2006 19:04:54 -0000

Are there any sites with information on edges first solving? I couldn't seem to find any. I am interested, other seeing how some have approached this. I can solve doing edges first, but it takes way too many moves for me to solve edges and the try and do the corners. Eric
317. Re: Edges First....
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 29 Nov 2006 08:28:47 -0000

Hi :-) There are no sites about edges-first solving that im aware of, and if there are they are most likely for speedsolving anyway. The basic approach to edges first, which may be what u have tried, is to do cross first then the middle layer by simple 3-move algs and then finally last layer also with very simple algs. This works for speeding but gives a high move count yes. To make it short one makes use of the given edge configuration, like checking if one face has 2 or more edges placed correctly wrt eachother and so on. Then explore many ways to do the last edge(s) on that layer while "picking other edges", and so forth. This just gives u an idea... it's a little bit more co mplicated than doing corners first because there are 12 edges versus 8 corners, but an edge has only 2 orientations versus 3 for corners. Most people find it not that hard to do corners first ignoring edges. edges first can be done ignoring corners completely. To get some corners along the way insert moves at appropriate places (usually one turn) to make a c/e pair that is not broken later. Or just reply on luck (trial end error) to get some corners. There's no secret recipe just like there's really no recipe for making petrus blocks either. One just SEES how to bring the cubies together. -Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...> wrote: > > Are there any sites with information on edges first solving? I couldn't > seem to find any. I am interested, other seeing how some have > approached this. I can solve doing edges first, but it takes way too > many moves for me to solve edges and the try and do the corners. > > Eric >

I am interested in getting a list of corner commutators/algs. Eric --- Per Kristen Fredlund <aspiring_to_love@...> wrote: > Hi :-) > > There are no sites about edges-first solving that im > aware of, and if > there are they are most likely for speedsolving > anyway. The basic > approach to edges first, which may be what u have > tried, is to do > cross first then the middle layer by simple 3-move > algs and then > finally last layer also with very simple algs. This > works for speeding > but gives a high move count yes. To make it short > one makes use of the > given edge configuration, like checking if one face > has 2 or more > edges placed correctly wrt eachother and so on. Then > explore many ways > to do the last edge(s) on that layer while "picking > other edges", and > so forth. This just gives u an idea... it's a little > bit more co > mplicated than doing corners first because there are > 12 edges versus 8 > corners, but an edge has only 2 orientations versus > 3 for corners. > Most people find it not that hard to do corners > first ignoring edges. > edges first can be done ignoring corners completely. > To get some > corners along the way insert moves at appropriate > places (usually one > turn) to make a c/e pair that is not broken later. > Or just reply on > luck (trial end error) to get some corners. There's > no secret recipe > just like there's really no recipe for making petrus > blocks either. > One just SEES how to bring the cubies together. > > -Per > > > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, > "ericdstalter" > <ericdstalter@...> wrote: > > > > Are there any sites with information on edges > first solving? 319. RE: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: Edges First....
From: "Daniel Harris" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: <fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com>
Date: Wed, 29 Nov 2006 19:17:46 -0000

Hi Eric, To solve the corners, you don't really need a list as such, you can make up commutators "on the fly" (as Per calls it) One form is the PQP'Q' commutator - for example (R U R') D (R U' R') D' - the Q part is always the opposite layer to the middle move in the P part. Do that on your cube and try to understand how it works. Then talk to Per :) It took me many days to grasp this concept, and I only managed it for these types of commutator. But I think there are many other useful (if slightly longer) forms which you could apply. my yahoo id is hatadey if you want to chat about this sometime :) Dan :) _____ From: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com [mailto:fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com] On Behalf Of eric stalter Sent: 29 November 2006 19:01 To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com Subject: Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: Edges First.... 322. Close to the likely shortest solution in QTM metric.
From: "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 03 Dec 2006 17:26:35 -0000

It is interesting that several best solvers started with B L' even without realizing the pre-moves F' R'. Actually, I was very close to the likely best solution: Do [B F' R'] before scramble, B L'_D R2 D'_ B F_D' L D_ F. U2 , all but 3 corners finished(!!!), insert F' D F U F' D' F U' at the dot and get B L' D R2 D' B F D' L D2 F U F' D' F U B F' R' (19, 21, 18) This might not be hard to find since I had those pre-moves. I missed such oportunity :-(. Mirek

326. Re: frustrating corners
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 05 Dec 2006 14:57:32 -0000

Hey Eric! yoiu can try sort out the duo-twist by using 2 inserted corner 3- cycles. The first cycle must use the 2 corners that should be twisted and ANY other corner. Orientation for this cycle will also not matter. So there is VERY good chances you will have good cancellations with the first one. For the second you do a strict 3- cycle to solve the 3 corners that were permuted with the first cycle. Now you require a bit more luck to get cancellations. But this way of doing it will most likely be better than inserting ONE alg to do the work ;-) -Per --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...> wrote: > > Ok > > Last week for the FMC I had a 23move solve, but had 2 corners twisted > wrong, they were in the right spot. This week I had another solve at > 24moves, but had 3 corners in the right spot w/incorrect orientation. > > Do most of you just go "oh well" and start in a new direction, cause I > only know 2 alg's that solve to twisted corners, but they are > 12/14moves long. > > temporarily frustrated > > Eric > > ps. I turned in this week's solution(I went a different way) and was > very lucky, had a normal mid-30move solve, but was able to cancel 8 > moves. so I got a sub-30 move count. >

329. Re: Edges first solution.
From: "Per Kristen Fredlund" <aspiring_to_love@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 18 Dec 2006 10:10:45 -0000

Hi Eric! I would say anything below 16 turns for edges first is good. As for corner insertions after that it depends a whole lot on luck. But usually there is at least one ok insertion (2 or more turns cancelled) when u have to do 2 insertions. It happens that i find no insertion for a single corner 3-cycle that will give any cancellation at all. But sometimes still save a turn or 2 coz at least u find a 8- turn insertion, whereas cycling those corners right at the end would have required 9 or 10 turns ;-) An edges first start with more than 5 corners to solve is not too useful unless extremely short, because 3 or more insertions will be needed, unless u get lucky and have 6 corners to sort out as 2 disjoint 3-cycle. A 3-cycle + a corner-twist is equivalent in terms of work to having a corner 5-cycle left to deal with :-) -Per Kristen PS! Yes Dan's site i don't get into properly anymore lately. Hope he can sort it out very soon :D > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...> wrote: > > This week I introduced my first edges first solution, with to corner > cycle insertions.
